## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: chemical kinetics
**Analysis**: This task models the rate of change of concentration of a chemical species as a function of time and concentration. The rate law dA/dt = f(A, t) describes how quickly a reactant is consumed or product is formed, governed by reaction order, mechanism complexity, and possible time-dependent effects.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A (rate proportional to concentration)
- Second-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (rate proportional to square of concentration)
- nth-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (general power-law rate dependence)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (forward and reverse first-order reactions with equilibrium)
- Reversible second-order: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 + c1 * A + c2 (quadratic rate with equilibrium terms)
- Mixed-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2 (combination of first and second order)
- Michaelis-Menten type: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) (enzyme-catalyzed or saturation kinetics)
- Autocatalytic: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (logistic-type autocatalytic reaction)
- Inhibition kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A**2) (substrate inhibition)
- Time-dependent decay: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (rate with time-dependent catalyst deactivation)
- Consecutive reaction: dA_dt = c0 * exp(c1 * t) + c2 * exp(c3 * t) (intermediate in consecutive reactions)
- Fractional order with offset: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 + c2 (fractional order with constant source/sink)
- Cooperative kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 / (c2 + A**c1) (Hill-type cooperative binding)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope ŌåÆ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects ŌåÆ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay ŌåÆ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior ŌåÆ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects ŌåÆ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Negative rate values (consumption) with magnitude increasing with concentration ŌåÆ simple power-law rate law dA_dt = -c * A**n with n > 0
- Rate approaching zero at long times while A approaches nonzero value ŌåÆ reversible reaction with equilibrium, includes constant offset term
- Rate proportional to A*(Amax - A) ŌåÆ autocatalytic mechanism with logistic-type dynamics
- Rate that saturates at high concentration ŌåÆ Michaelis-Menten rational form c*A/(K+A)
- Rate that peaks then decreases with increasing A ŌåÆ substrate inhibition, rational form with A**2 in denominator
- Linear relationship between dA_dt and A ŌåÆ first-order kinetics, slope gives rate constant
- Rate depends on both A and t explicitly ŌåÆ time-varying rate constant due to temperature change, catalyst deactivation, or photochemical effects
- Multiple exponential timescales visible in data ŌåÆ coupled or consecutive reactions with multiple rate constants
- Rate proportional to product of concentration terms like A*(c-A) ŌåÆ bimolecular reaction where second species is stoichiometrically linked to A

**GT numerical expression:** `-0.6789593965981179*A**2 - 0.6789593965981179*A + 0.1640697849676163*sin(log(A + 1))`

The GT has three terms:
1. A quadratic term: `-0.6790*A┬▓`
2. A linear term: `-0.6790*A`

Key observations:
- The GT is a function of A only (no t dependence)
- It contains: A┬▓, A, and sin(log(A+1))
- No A┬│ term, no exponential terms, no log terms (other than inside sin)

Let me analyze each candidate. For candidates with `t`, I need to check if the `t`-dependent terms can be zeroed out.

**Candidates with `log(c*exp(A*c) + 1)` terms:** This is a softplus-like function. For this to vanish or become polynomial, we'd need special constants. If c_coefficient = 0, the log term becomes log(c5+1) = constant. So these terms can be absorbed into a constant. But then we lose the sin(log(A+1)) term unless it appears elsewhere.

Let me focus on candidates that contain `sin(c*log(A*c + 1) + c)` since this is the key basis function in GT.
